        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2206800450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13858980134757414024">This book is so slow at the beginning, almost nothing happened for the first 200 pages, before things picked up and revelations started blowing my mind. I didn’t like the way the author explains the magic system, when you’re reading a very interesting part of the book and one of the characters starts drafting(i.e the magic), the author will stop the dialogue and start explaining the magic, that was done throughout the book, I still don’t know the limits of the magic. The battle scenes in this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText13858980134757414024" style="display:none">This book is so slow at the beginning, almost nothing happened for the first 200 pages, before things picked up and revelations started blowing my mind. I didn’t like the way the author explains the magic system, when you’re reading a very interesting part of the book and one of the characters starts drafting(i.e the magic), the author will stop the dialogue and start explaining the magic, that was done throughout the book, I still don’t know the limits of the magic. The battle scenes in this book are astounding, I love even single one of them, especially that of Karris.<br /><br /><u>Magic System</u><br />This is very complex, its a bit complex than that of Brandon Sanderson, it was not well explained which made some parts quite confusing, I understand most parts of how the magic works apart from the transportation, that part is still unclear to me. The magic is use for everything, buildings, clothings' weapons and transportation. The magic caste is divided into four, someone that can draft one colour is known as a monochrome, two biochrome, three polychrome and all seven colours a Prism. Colours are used for magic like Biochroma in Warbreaker but colours are used more here.<br /><br /><u>World building and Writing</u><br />The author did an amazing job with the world, especially the Chrometia, I really like the way the author depicted that, Garriston, Rekton and the rest are not bad either. The book is written in third person multiple POVs of very interesting characters, its comprehensible with amazing dialogues.<br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br />The Guile brothers: Gavin Guile is the emperor and priest of the seven Satraps, he is also a Prism, he had ruled for 16 years so far and is almost at the end of his reign. Gavin is quite a jovial guy, knows his way with politics and battles. Dazen is Gavin’s younger brother, and also the better brother in my opinion, despite his past.<br /><br />Kip is a 15 year old, whose life got turned upside down after a major revelation and an ordeal. Even at that he still weathered it and came out a stronger and better person. Kip has a very low self esteem partly cause he is fat and also cause of his mother.<br /><br />Karris is the badass female character, despite her being 32, everyone talks about her beautiful she is, I love her so much. She is neither bitchy nor annoying, she is confident without being rude and kind.<br /><br />Liv, I loathe her, I want her to just die, from the first time she was introduced in the book, I knew she was going to be a problem, just another self righteous, know it all bitch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13858980134757414024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2906195175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2906195175" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2906195175?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316246279" href="/book/show/16131107-the-black-prism">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906195175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15013933963071033495">This is a re-read for me, but I am oh so happy to be back in this world which I first encountered in 2015. As the series draws to its close (book #5 is due out later this year) I decided to do a #LightbringerSeriesReread to re-familiarise myself with the world, characters and magic. It turns out I still remembered the majority of the magic, and yet going back to the series I found it so much easier from the start to actually 'get' what was happening because I had that bit more familiarity. I thi</span>
  <span id="freeText15013933963071033495" style="display:none">This is a re-read for me, but I am oh so happy to be back in this world which I first encountered in 2015. As the series draws to its close (book #5 is due out later this year) I decided to do a #LightbringerSeriesReread to re-familiarise myself with the world, characters and magic. It turns out I still remembered the majority of the magic, and yet going back to the series I found it so much easier from the start to actually 'get' what was happening because I had that bit more familiarity. I think at first this series throws you in at the deep end, but once you get to know what's what you start to understand the differences in the magic and see the start of the alliances and politics which later come into play.<br /><br />I had forgotten exactly what point certain things got revealed in this series, and it turns out that some of the biggest things happen right in book #1 where I was happy to rediscover the same amazement and awe at the brashness and bold defiance of some of these characters. I still felt like Kip was a bit of a wuss to start out, but I know there is a lot of growing to be done over the course of the books, and I look forward to following his adventure.<br /><br />Karys (spellings may be wrong as I audiobooked) is one of the characters I liked the most in book #1 as she is feisty and doesn't take anything from anyone. She's not afraid to slap the Prism or defy gender stereotypes and she does so with style. I still think her plotline works really well as a counter to some of the others, and I am glad we get to see her inner emotions as a viewpoint.<br /><br />I think Liv is a character who I like at first, but as the book goes further her ideals started to bother me a little more and I remembered her a little more fondly than I now think of her. She's certainly not a character who I would have thought had as much involvement when thinking back, but actually in this story she is very much central to seeing how Kip's storyline develops. <br /><br />Kip and Gavin are super powerful and both have the wit and snark which I remember this book for. They have charisma and charm and they can work their way out of crazy situations, but they also have a knack for getting into terrible situations. I must admit to liking both, but finding both so silly too :D<br /><br />I enjoyed seeing Corbin and Ironfist a little in this plot as they feel like more minor characters but they have a major impact on our main characters quite often. I really enjoyed their stories and the way that they were integrated. <br /><br />Overall, the pacing and plot were fantastic and I definitely felt like there was a lot to love about this series on the re-read. It's definitely a series I 100% recommend and as long as you're prepared to learn a new magic system and wrap your head around politics and lots of characters then I think you will love it. 5*s on the re-read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15013933963071033495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1387502974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1387502974" />
    <a title="Lema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18145934-lema"><img alt="Lema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507843225p2/18145934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1387502974?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lema" href="/user/show/18145934-lema">Lema</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316246279" href="/book/show/16131107-the-black-prism">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1387502974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18110349625017927625">Wow just wow... So many great fantasy novels I've been stumbling upon lately. I usually reserve the high expectations for any <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson' title='Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brandon Sanderson</a> novel, but I was amazed by the beauty and fluidity in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6524620.Brian_McClellan' title='Brian McClellan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brian McClellan</a> books, and now this evil genius <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1370283.Brent_Weeks' title='Brent Weeks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brent Weeks</a> comes along... Sure, he needs to work on his description capabilities, since several of my friends and I had the exact same comments about the exact same parts then I doubt that we all lack the imagination. Other than that, pure evil genius..</span>
  <span id="freeText18110349625017927625" style="display:none">Wow just wow... So many great fantasy novels I've been stumbling upon lately. I usually reserve the high expectations for any <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" title="Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandon Sanderson</a> novel, but I was amazed by the beauty and fluidity in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6524620.Brian_McClellan" title="Brian McClellan" rel="nofollow noopener">Brian McClellan</a> books, and now this evil genius <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1370283.Brent_Weeks" title="Brent Weeks" rel="nofollow noopener">Brent Weeks</a> comes along... Sure, he needs to work on his description capabilities, since several of my friends and I had the exact same comments about the exact same parts then I doubt that we all lack the imagination. Other than that, pure evil genius..Brava!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380298363ra/682847.gif" width="400" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So let's dissect this, first of all <u>
  <i>The PLOT</i>
</u>:<br>Now that I think about it, I don't believe the synopsis here has done the real plot any justice (which is a mark of a successful synopsis for me since I HATE unnecessary plot reveals), Gavin Guile discovering that he has a bastard son is only a tiny fraction of the beginning of a highly complex, wide-reaching cascade of events. There is no clear quest and no clear villain to fight off, but everything was so fast-paced with so many little hells breaking loose all over, it'll just sucks you right in and never lets you go. Not to mention the plot twists..no no not plot twists, more like existential crises that makes you want to reread everything and revise your values.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479570446ra/21208368.gif" width="300" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As for the <u>
  <i>WORLD BUILDING</i>
</u> I kinda had a love/hate relationship with it the first part of the book because boy can Brent Weeks go on and on describing modes of transportation, bridges and walls that after finishing the first book still resemble shapeless blobs of color in my head. <br>Not to mention the sizable info dump that was thrust upon us, I was quite disoriented for like 200 pages and that was me basically..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479569054i/21208177._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="420" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>However, it was still enjoyable to read about the world in general because it was simply amazing. It oozes Assassin's Creed vibes, and I absolutely loved the whole concept of the Chromeria and Chromaturgy school setting, and I believe in that instance, the author has done an amazing job in describing the Jaspers isles. <br><br>Now to my favorite part...<u>
  <i>CHARACTERS:</i>
</u> we have two main POVs:<br><b>Gavin Guile</b> you sneaky bastard! you thoroughly stole my heart. <br>That guy is the epitome of a most interesting character, to put it briefly: he's a charismatic asshole, with a hidden agenda and a heart of gold. His personality is so layered that that I still feel like I know everything and nothing about him, and I can't wait to read more and find out about every dirty little secret he's hiding.<br><br><b>Kip</b> at first he comes across as the lovable doofus and the comic relief of the series. I was ok with him at first and found him to be a hilarious version of Neville Longbottom. But again, as I read more about him and discovered more about his past I couldn't but love him and want to protect him at all cost. I actually liked how damaged he is, because usually we read about these protagonists who had a horrible upbringing but have this stellar generic personality with absolutely no scratches whatsoever..Not Kip no, and it was awesome reading about his journey fighting his demons.<br><br>We also have three minor POVs:<br><b>Karris</b>: I just love her sections, typical independent ass-kicking woman in her thirties who takes shit from no one and least of all from Gavin. Her past is so turbulent adding more mystery to her and I feel her personality still have so much more room for future development.<br><br><b>The prisoner</b>: Definitely the highlight of the book, I'll say no more other than make sure that you are not eating or drinking while reading these sections. <br><br><b>Liv</b>: she's interesting, and I really sympathize with her and appreciate the inner-conflicts she's going through. No feels avalanche though..yet.<br><br>Of course there are many other minor characters that are the cherry on top of this mouthwatering cake, like <b>Ironfist</b>: the blackguard commander, and <b>Corvan Danavis</b>: the brilliant general in exile and Liv's father. <br><br><b>In conclusion, amazing characters, unique world and magical system, hilarious conversations, heart-wrenching scenes, mystery, secrets, intrigue, dark pasts, slow start but absolutely totally WORTH IT!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479567997ra/21208051.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="18110349625017927625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_298658298" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298658298" />
    <a title="Mpauli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8323869-mpauli"><img alt="Mpauli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373482375p2/8323869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298658298?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mpauli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mpauli" href="/user/show/8323869-mpauli">Mpauli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8517437-the-black-prism">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=rating_2-stars">rating_2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=genre_fantasy">genre_fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=genre_epic-fantasy">genre_epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=genre_flintlock-fantasy">genre_flintlock-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=orga_read-in-2014">orga_read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298658298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15746043050311838995">The Black Prism is the first installment in Brent Weeks' second series called Lightbringer. It's an Epic Fantasy with some of the typical ingredients you would expect, but all is kind of twisted to the author's unique style and your enjoyment of the book will highly depend on how much that style works for you.<br/><br/>In total we're following 7 characters, 2 of them being the main protagonists, 2 with a decent amount of "screen-time" and 3 with only a few chapters.<br/>The first of the two main characters is </span>
  <span id="freeText15746043050311838995" style="display:none">The Black Prism is the first installment in Brent Weeks' second series called Lightbringer. It's an Epic Fantasy with some of the typical ingredients you would expect, but all is kind of twisted to the author's unique style and your enjoyment of the book will highly depend on how much that style works for you.<br /><br />In total we're following 7 characters, 2 of them being the main protagonists, 2 with a decent amount of "screen-time" and 3 with only a few chapters.<br />The first of the two main characters is Kip. Kip is an over-weight 15 year old who lives in a small town called Rekton in Tyrea. Tyrea is one of 7 satrapies that make up a huge nation. <br />The spiritual leader of this nation is Gavin, the Prism. He is the most powerful wizard of the land and can wield all different kinds of colors.<br />Colors? Yes, Brent Weeks uses a very interesting magic system based on 7 primary colors, each with slighly different attributes. Most mages can only use one or two colors and a few can use even more. I don't want to go into too much detail about the magic system, cause one of the fun things of the book is to learn that system during the novel.<br /><br />In addition to the male main heroes Kip and Gavin, Weeks gives us two female heroines as well, but they are less prominent characters.<br />Karris White Oak is one of the Blackguard, an elite force of bodyguards charged with protecting the Prism. Her relationship to the prism is complicated, cause they were actually betrothed in the past.<br />Last, but not least we have Liv, who is a student at the Chromeria, the large spiritual center of the nation, where the Prism resides and the drafters, that's what mages are called here, are schooled. Originally she's from the same village Kip comes from.<br /><br />As you might see from the setup with a teenage boy from a village and a powerful sorcerer, we tread on familiar Epic Fantasy ground, although the author tries to spin the usual tropes a bit.<br />The world-building and the magic system are intriguing and were some of my favorite parts of the book.<br />Unfortunately, the other parts weren't without flaws for me. My main complaint with the book is the actual writing style. When it's good it is very staright forward, but when it's bad, then it seems really clumsy.<br />Too often Weeks looses himself in endless descriptions of trivial things. A broom closet can be described in 3 pages, and the way he describes motion can be very tedious. There are outstretched arms that pull water away...thanks I know how swimming works. "He swam" would have been fine.<br />With over 600 pages this book is fairly long and for my taste a few less of these descriptions would have worked in favor of the novel.<br />A second thing is internal monologue. There are scenes like this: "Kip didn't want to stare at her chest now for the second time. Third time. Stop staring, maybe only a final fourth time. Oops five."<br />This is not an actual quote, but it's very close. Especially the word "Oops" is used a couple of times.<br />This all comes from one effort. Brent Weeks wants to use humor constantly. But he's not writing a parody (actually I think this could have been a great 350p parody, if he would have embraced it).<br />Where other authors use singular characters for comic relief, Weeks uses every single one of his main cast and thus hurts their credibility. <br />And it gets worse. Another thing he really likes is ultra-brutal over-the-top violence out of nowhere. The novel, especially with how silly, snarky and funny every character is, often reads like a very light-hearted PG 13 book. But then, all of a sudden, heads are rolling, limbs are chopped of and there is violence for a short amount of time...and then everything goes back to normal.<br />Kip sees a lot of violence in the beginning, but only 1-2 days after that female breasts and snarky one-liners are all he can think about. As a reader I never had the feeling that the violence really got to the characters, neither if they were on the receiving or giving end.<br />Imagine an episode of Grey's Anatomy where Meredith and Christina are chatting about boys, then an axe murderer runs into the hospital, kills and mutilates 50 people, is then killed brutally by Meredith with a scalpel and 5 minutes later while his entrails are still over her coat, she says to Christina: "This McDreamy guy is hot, isn't he?"<br /><br />So, overall the book lacks decisiveness in my opinion. The balance between description and plot doesn't work well, the decision if it is humorous or serious is often answered with "Whatever the author was in the mood for" and therefore the characters lack focus as well and are torn between roles.<br />I think Weeks had good intentions and wanted to play with tropes, but for me his execution doesn't work. <br />I haven't read his first series, so if you are a fan of the Night Angel books and don't have so many stylistic issues as I have, then I think you will enjoy this book, cause -as I said- your enjoyment will highly depend on how much you like the author's style. <br />It isn't a hopeless case and the plot is solid, the world-building is very good and although this read was only okay for me, I'm going to continue with the series, but not just right away. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15746043050311838995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_401676929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/401676929" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/401676929?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8517437-the-black-prism">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=flintlock-fantasy">flintlock-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer401676929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15363853626803774458">Well paced. Deceptively complex plot, characters and history. Unique and well defined magic system. Intriguing mysteries to be solved. Rewards those who pay attention to detail, which also gives it reread value to catch those details that were skimmed or dismissed the first time round. Held my attention. Surprised me quite a few times. Thoroughly enjoyable.<br/><br/>The magic system in this book, called <i>Chromaturgy,</i> is second to nothing I’ve read to date – and that includes Sanderson’s Mistborn Trilogy, w</span>
  <span id="freeText15363853626803774458" style="display:none">Well paced. Deceptively complex plot, characters and history. Unique and well defined magic system. Intriguing mysteries to be solved. Rewards those who pay attention to detail, which also gives it reread value to catch those details that were skimmed or dismissed the first time round. Held my attention. Surprised me quite a few times. Thoroughly enjoyable.<br /><br />The magic system in this book, called <i>Chromaturgy,</i> is second to nothing I’ve read to date – and that includes Sanderson’s Mistborn Trilogy, which I thought was the Bomb as far as magic systems go. Chromaturgy involves the harnessing of light energy and converting it to matter, a substance called Luxin, which manifests in different forms depending on what colour you “draft.” Interesting combinations can be used in constructing building materials or for combat for devastating effect. <br /><br />Most “drafters” are “Monochromes” ie born with the ability to draft a specific colour, some can draft two colours (Bichromes) and rarer again are those who can draft several colours (Polychromes). Each colour also has an associated personality trait/attribute which manifests while drafting eg Red = anger, blue=cool logic, yellow =clarity of thought etc. Only one person has the ability to draft every colour – The Prism.<br /><br />Having recently read Sanderson’s Mistborn, the comparison of the two magic systems seems inevitable given that there are some striking similarities between Chromaturgy and Allomancy. Chromaturgy uses a spectrum of 7 colours and uses light to fuel its magic – while Mistborn’s Allomancy uses 14(+2 unknown) metals to fuel its magic users. Both systems have well defined rules and limitations eg with Chromaturgy, drafting light will eventually send the drafter insane (referred to as “breaking the halo”) turning them into a “colour wight.” Drafter’s who “break the halo” are euthanized. But whereas Sanderson meticulously lays out the rules through the narration using constant repetition, Weeks allows the reader to discover the various rules and applications of Chromaturgy through inference from the action, and dialogue, which I think is a lot more fun. So which is better? I’m undecided as yet.<br /><br />Religion plays a large role in the book as well and I found the Theology and how it ties into the magic system and politics quite interesting. The Satrapies worship the god Orholom as part of a monotheistic religion. So there are a lot of similarities and parallels to Catholicism. The Prism is like the Pope(albeit not a very believing one). They have a parallel to the sign of the cross but involving seven parts instead of three. Detractors are referred to as pagans or worshipping pagan gods. The major plot element involving Gavin and Dazen also has parallels to the Biblical story of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jacob and Esau. I didn't see it till later in the story when we meet Gavin's parents. The blind father. The knowing mother. The switch. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I'm not sure if it was deliberate, but the similarities are so striking I found it hard to ignore. Especially when once I saw it I started seeing a lot of other religious parallels clicking into place and it really added to the depth of the world building.<br /><br />The story takes place in “The Seven Satrapies” seven countries ruled from the Chromeria by a council called “The Spectrum” which is headed by “The White” with “The Prism,” Gavin Guile as the figurehead Head of state. As the story unfolds we learn the history of the Seven Satrapies, the politics and intrigue of the court, and a dark secret kept for sixteen years by the reigning Prism. A secret so damning that if discovered, Gavin Guile could upset a delicate balance that has kept the realm at an uneasy peace since he deposed his brother Dazen Guile in The False Prism War. The politics and intrigue and twists just keep coming as we slowly unravel the truth about the past and what really happened at the famous battle of Sundered Rock. <br /><br />The story ends well – or as well as a “to be continued” can. We are left with a mystery and with a sense of foreboding that things are about to change drastically for our Prism. The book left me thinking on the various elements when I was finished. Even the title of the book left me with the question, What or who is “The Black Prism” referring to? Is it a false Prism? Or an evil Prism? Or a morally flawed Prism? Or a dark skinned Prism? Its that sort of cryptic approach to the story that really adds to the enjoyment.<br /><br />I’d like to give this a 7 for the 7 colours – but goodreads only has 5 stars. I will be most definitely continuing the series with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12499290.The_Blinding_Knife__Lightbringer___2_" title="The Blinding Knife (Lightbringer, #2) by Brent Weeks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blinding Knife</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15363853626803774458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1730415382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1730415382" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1730415382?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789546554840" href="/book/show/21941789">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=advanture">advanture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=brent-weeks">brent-weeks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730415382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2339452286541685732"><b>*** 4.85 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with Eon and Sarah La Luna @ the Mecca for Fantasy on GR, BB&B!!! </b><br/><br/>Epic! Not just the genre of Fantasy, but the book itself - EPIC!!! Brent Weeks has taken the torch of Epic Fantasy with some traditional leanings and is finding his way into our hearts and Favorites Book Shelves.... I am in awe of the magical system BW has chosen to base this World on and am fascinated by the different cultures and how their ethnological and physical differences are conducive to one aspect</span>
  <span id="freeText2339452286541685732" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.85 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with Eon and Sarah La Luna @ the Mecca for Fantasy on GR, BB&amp;B!!! </b><br /><br />Epic! Not just the genre of Fantasy, but the book itself - EPIC!!! Brent Weeks has taken the torch of Epic Fantasy with some traditional leanings and is finding his way into our hearts and Favorites Book Shelves.... I am in awe of the magical system BW has chosen to base this World on and am fascinated by the different cultures and how their ethnological and physical differences are conducive to one aspect of the magic or another.... One thing is obvious - Brent Weeks is setting up the stage for a grand adventure, a story for the ages, a major battle of Good, Evil, and all those many hews in between... <br /><br />Chromeria. It is the land of 7 Satrupies/States, governed by satrups, all under the umbrella of Chromeria and its ruling body of 7 Colors drafters, a Black, a White, and the highest placed, kind of like an Emperor - The Prism. At this time The Prism is Gavin Guile and he can draft all the Colors in the rainbow. You see, in this world the magic is based on light and the way it makes the eye perceive it and then translate it into colors. Those who have been born with the ability to take in the light of any color and pull it into their body cells, then learn how to shape the byproduct, luxin, into some useful form, those are the Drafters, the magicians of their world. They are blessed, live well, fast, and early on succumb to madness and death... Everyone knows the score, the whole system has been shaped to accommodate those limitations. Each generation there is only one Prism born, the person who brings balance to the Color-system Magic and the defacto Pope and Emperor... Or at least, there SHOULD be only one, until Gavin and his brother, Dazen Guile. And with them came the War of the Prisms.... <br /><br />The magic system is intricate and complex, but it is amazing, especially once you get used to the character of the different colors and the way the magic can be drafted and utilized. The characters are introduced as the action builds and by the end, when things are hectic and nerve wracking, we know and already root for the ones we get to know best - Gavin, the lady he is crazy about Karris, and Kip, the chubby, hormone riddled, clumsy, awkward, and extremely inappropriate teenager with a Haze addict for a mother, and a father he just learns about, who is lost, has lost everything he has known, and now is absolutely confused as to what he is supposed to do, learn or be from now on.... Yes, Kip is the typical young man of the Classical Fantasy Genre, on his requisite journey to discover himself and fight to be as good as he can be, while fighting temptation and the darkness within. It is a cliche, yes, but it is THE cliche we keep coming back for time and again, craving for one more time, at least in Fantasy, for the good guys to learn their lessons and come back on top. This is why we read this genre, isn't it??? <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"... Kip had made his oaths to the living and to the dead. He gritted his teeth, sure he was making the wrong decision—and making it anyway. It’s better that the innocent should live than that the guilty die....</b>
</i><br /><br />It is all about choices, guilt, and secrets. It is GLORIOUS! <br /><br />I will recommend this to all the Fantasy fans. The beginning is a bit slow, until you get used to the complex magic system, but after that it is all easy sailing, so don't give up on it, it is sooooo worth it! And as a person who has had extensive color theory at school, I can only say that if such drafting was possible, this would be as close to the characteristics of the colors as it could get! Fascinating, engaging and filled with action - what more can you ask for???<br /><br />I wish you all Happy Reading and may you never stop believing in the fantastical!!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="2339452286541685732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2947951369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2947951369" />
    <a title="Jody " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41767362-jody"><img alt="Jody " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558120407p2/41767362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2947951369?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316246279" href="/book/show/16131107-the-black-prism">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2947951369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1887847150318366448"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Light cannot be chained."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>To say the <i>Lightbringer</i> series has been on my TBR list for a while would be a huge understatement. A few months ago I noticed the last book in the series was coming out this year, and I knew it was time to finally delve into this once and for all. <br/><br/>The setting of this story is a land called The Seven Satrapies. A satrapy is basically a province that is governed by a person known as a satrap. The Chromeria is the ruling body of the Seven Satrapies, and also wh</span>
  <span id="freeText1887847150318366448" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Light cannot be chained."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />To say the <i>Lightbringer</i> series has been on my TBR list for a while would be a huge understatement. A few months ago I noticed the last book in the series was coming out this year, and I knew it was time to finally delve into this once and for all. <br /><br />The setting of this story is a land called The Seven Satrapies. A satrapy is basically a province that is governed by a person known as a satrap. The Chromeria is the ruling body of the Seven Satrapies, and also where all of the drafters, magical users, are trained. <br /><br />The magic in this series is quite unique. It is called drafting and requires the magic user to take a specific color of light from the color spectrum and transform it into magic. A drafter may able to draft only one color, or they can draft multiple colors. The more colors, the more useful you are to the Chromeria. Not to mention being more powerful. The magic system took me a while to get used to. It is very detailed and I really didn't get the feel for it until I was near the end. It is really cool stuff though once you figure it out. <br /><br /><i>Monochrome - Can only draft one color.<br />Bichrome - Can draft two colors.<br />Polychrome - Can draft more than two colors.<br />Full spectrum Polychrome - Can draft all colors in the visual color spectrum.</i><br /><br />If the world building and characters in <i>The Black Prism</i> are any indication of what is to come, then this is going to be a really good series. The story so far is mainly focused on the after effects of an event that happened 15 years before known as The Prism's War. Secrets are being revealed and old alliances are forming again. But 15 years is a good amount of time. There are new players in the game now. Not to mention, those that would do anything for revenge.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"At some point, you have to decide not merely what you're going to believe, but how you're going to believe. Are you going to believe in people, or in ideas? With your heart, or with your head? Will you believe what's in fornt of you, or in what you think you know? There are some things you think you know that are lies. I can't tell you what those are, and I'm sorry for that."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />These characters are fleshed out very well and each has their own distinct voice. So much so, that it was hard for me to pick a favorite. The chapters are very short, and you're constantly bouncing back and forth between story lines. So, the usual just one more chapter turns into 5 or 6. At least it did for me. Gavin Guile (The Prism) and Kip get the most page time. Kip was easy to route for from the beginning. I thought Gavin was a bit of a bastard at the beginning, but he started to grown on me throughout the story. There is also Alviana, Karris, and Dazen just to name a few more that get there own chapters. It is a good size cast of characters, but most of them are side characters. It's not hard to keep up with them at all. <br /><br /><i>The Black Prism</i> was a fantastic start to this series. The magic system takes a while to figure out, but it's so cool once it clicks. The world building focuses on the history of this world as much as the present, and that really won me over. Well rounded characters that have their own identity and are not without fault. I can't wait to see where this story goes. If you haven't read the available books in this series so far, I strongly urge you to remedy that as fast as possible.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"The Philosopher said that a man alone is either a god or a monster......I'm no god."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 4.5 stars ****</b> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1887847150318366448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3110925685" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3110925685" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3110925685?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/32812493-the-black-prism">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3110925685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14201377258527582165"><blockquote>
  <i>All power is a test.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I wouldn't have picked this series up if it wasn't for my friend and buddy-reader, Brad, being a fanboy. To put it in his words: this isn't reinventing the wheel (aka doing something completely new) but it's one of the best popcorn-fiction (fantasy) out there. <br/><br/>This world has a weird magic system. Colours mean magical power. There are drafters who can manipulate a colour or two, shape tools or weapons with them. Every colour means something different (green being wild, red</span>
  <span id="freeText14201377258527582165" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>All power is a test.</i>
</blockquote><br />I wouldn't have picked this series up if it wasn't for my friend and buddy-reader, Brad, being a fanboy. To put it in his words: this isn't reinventing the wheel (aka doing something completely new) but it's one of the best popcorn-fiction (fantasy) out there. <br /><br />This world has a weird magic system. Colours mean magical power. There are drafters who can manipulate a colour or two, shape tools or weapons with them. Every colour means something different (green being wild, red mostly full of temperament, blue being cooly calculating etc). Some are even able to draft more than one colour. And then there is the Prism. One who can control all the colours. Gavin Guile is the Prism.<br />But he harbours quite the secret. Truth be told, I figured it out very early on in the book. But that didn't diminish the payoff when it was actually revealed to the reader. <br />There's been a war between Gavin and his younger brother, Dazen. The Prism's War. Afterwards, the Prism has been stripped of his political powers and has been demoted to the post of councellor, a ceremonial showpony (albeit with one hell of a lot of power). He still commands the respect of many simply because he is a good man. Not a perfect man, that would be entirely unrealistic, but one who cares about the people he's responsible for. <br />Moreover, his job is to keep the balance between the colours. You see, if one colour is drafted (used) too much and another not enough, all hell breaks loose in this world. But, soon enough, all colours are indeed used aplenty when a self-appointed king starts moving against the powers that be (the Chromeria) and the Prism himself since "his kingdom" had originally been on the side of the other Guile brother.<br /><br />Since this would all be far too easy, there are also the personal stories of a number of characters: <br />- The Prism with his former fiancée, Karris, who is a badass Black Guard with quite the mouth on her. I loved how she wasn't just beautiful, not just talented, not just had a very colourful backstory (see what I just did there? ;P) - she had as many facets as the rainbow, could be vulnerable as well as brave and I was so here for that (I'm tired of those fake-as-fuck female heroes who never make any mistakes and are only allowed to ever feel awesome and confident and shit and never make any mistakes).<br />- Gavin's bastard son, Kip, coming from an affair during his betrothal to Karris. There were many things obvious about him as well, but I still liked that he was a little atypical in many situations and yet, simultaneously, the typical teenager. I can only repeat myself: I like my characters realistic.<br />- Liv and her father. (Yes, there is a reason why I don't talk more about them. Just this much: Liv is an idiot.)<br />- Andros Guile and his wife (the Prism's parents). One a cold-blooded asshole, the other an extremely intelligent woman who had lost at least one son too many.<br />- The wights. (Can't give away too much about them, either, but the magic principle behind them is awesome; as is how they come to be and what it could mean.)<br /><br />Layer upon layer upon layer of lies and half-truths and betrayals, politics, people trying to manipulate others, some with money and power, some (supposedly) for love ... I swear, as is so often the case, too many things would have been more easily resolved if people had just talked to one another! That's actually the only complaint I have because this trope is a pet peeve of mine (in real life too).<br /><br />The writing, while not being extraordinarily beautiful or special, was very good and the author definitely knows how to weave a complex tale full of twists and turns. Moreover, the action was just as breathtaking as our tour through parts of this world was fascinating (like the school where Liv was instructed). I like it when the worldbuilding and the action balance each other out and this author pulled it off very well. So I can't agree with those who claim this has a slow start because every world needs an introduction and this is definitely not a bad or boring one.<br /><br />Story: fantastic. Writing: great. No real complaints from me and I'm curious to see where all the different <s>light beams</s> threads will lead. So much still to explore, too!<br /><blockquote>Sometimes, you need to squish a motherfucker.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14201377258527582165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3159692452?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda Waworga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda Waworga" href="/user/show/62212312-brenda-waworga">Brenda Waworga</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316246279" href="/book/show/16131107-the-black-prism">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3159692452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10907737841357868173">I swear i never read an epic Fantasy book centered so much on <b>PHYSICAL TRAITS</b> like i read on this book (example: breast and fat got mention so many times) <br/><br/>Now start with things I love from this book… I really love the magic system, it reminds me a lot with “WARBREAKER” by Brandon Sanderson (which i really love) but with so much more details, people have the ability to get power from colors, those colors also can produce certain shape and smell and have unique characterizations, it took me a long</span>
  <span id="freeText10907737841357868173" style="display:none">I swear i never read an epic Fantasy book centered so much on <b>PHYSICAL TRAITS</b> like i read on this book (example: breast and fat got mention so many times) <br /><br />Now start with things I love from this book… I really love the magic system, it reminds me a lot with “WARBREAKER” by Brandon Sanderson (which i really love) but with so much more details, people have the ability to get power from colors, those colors also can produce certain shape and smell and have unique characterizations, it took me a long time to understand it because it was just so complex! It also felt infodumpy , you need to learn and remember a lot of things on the first 300 pages. I also love the idea about the worldbuilding (Seven Satrapies surround The Cerulean Sea) and The Chromeria.<br /><br />Now onto the things I really REALLY DISLIKE… the way the author described and treated FEMALE CHARACTERS, THEY MAKE ME <b>CRINGE SO.MANY.TIMES</b>, I can handle some sexist/sexualized lines in fantasy book.. but there are just too many in this book, they really kill my enjoyment to read the story. <br /><br />I also don't like any of the character in this book, Gavin did so many horrible decisions and i just cannot root for him, Kip is a teenager with raging hormones, Karris describes as a badass female character but all she did is whinny about her ex from 15 years ago and when she got important mission, she got caught, Liv is another useless bland a bit dumb female character <br /><br />Sad I don’t like this book as much as I wanted to .. some of my friends said, the author's style didn’t change much through the series about the way he describe and treat women, so I guess I will just stop here and not continue read this series<br /><br /><b>2.5⭐️</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7698910335283063636"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Thesis and PhD applications are taking turns driving me in an early grave, so in lieu of a proper review, here are a random assortment of thoughts from the mind that brought you Cynical Natalie and Nice Natalie. <br/><br/>(P.S. They’re still alive. Nice Natalie is knitting booties in preparations for Christmas, and Cynical Natalie is stockpiling coal as projectiles)<br/><br/>✨Kip reminds me of Samwell Tarly, if Sam had a penchant for bad jokes at inopportune moments <br/>✨”Locke opened his mouth to say somethin</span>
  <span id="freeText7698910335283063636" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br><br>Thesis and PhD applications are taking turns driving me in an early grave, so in lieu of a proper review, here are a random assortment of thoughts from the mind that brought you Cynical Natalie and Nice Natalie. <br><br>(P.S. They’re still alive. Nice Natalie is knitting booties in preparations for Christmas, and Cynical Natalie is stockpiling coal as projectiles)<br><br>✨Kip reminds me of Samwell Tarly, if Sam had a penchant for bad jokes at inopportune moments <br>✨”Locke opened his mouth to say something ill-advised” from Scott Lynch’s The Lies of Locke Lamora is Kip in a single sentence <br>✨The magic system is cool and complex and too much for my overworked brain to handle atm<br>✨The Prism is the Avatar. Fight me<br>✨Actually the whole world is very much like the 4 elements. Drafters have temperaments who adhere to their color. Green represents wildness, for instance<br>✨Why is there slut-shaming??<br>✨Really why? Why does Liv need to comment on some bitchy classmate’s cleavage <br>✨Do men just look at their beloved and think how beautiful she is, for the 1000th time, even when there’s a war going on? Yes, Karris is beautiful. Liv is beautiful. We get it<br>✨Kip’s pubescent mood swings<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540959086ra/26525147.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✨GAVIN BRAGGING ABOUT LASTING ALL NIGHT<br>✨And so the Prism invented the first technicolor movie. He will shortly be hearing from Walt Disney’s lawyers<br>✨The whole marriage thing with King whatshisface. Classic villain move<br>✨Do I get a prize for guessing one of the plot twists? If so, can it be pink?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540959086ra/26525148.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✨Green golem=hulk smash<br>✨I wish we had flashback chapters<br>✨Liv, stop lusting after Gavin. He’s more than twice your age <br>✨That prison is on fleek<br><br>That is all. Also, emoji stars are shiny ✨✨✨✨✨</span>
  <a data-text-id="7698910335283063636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/JiA4IQVkhkwyxRTKZQEZiwaSG5X0qyfthvkMOhDMJ6LVBrjX/uVMFZwfZLHI/kWxA5LF6dz4qCapSKDsG72MA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5J9MatROum1V7ByAYl7+r7QfbBNIwz2XTHzCHUkseYaTU9ZpD6C9RDNXdUGM6QPfXAtvarhic6hgwgSuEQG/KA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText4180547241990862495" style="display:none">In a small-town Montana school at age 12, Brent Weeks met the two great loves of his life. Edgar Allan Poe introduced him to the power of literature to transcend time and death and loneliness. Fate introduced him to The Girl, Kristi Barnes. He began his pursuit of each immediately.<br /><br />The novel was a failure. The Girl shot him down.<br /><br />Since then–skipping the boring parts–Brent has written eight best-selling novels with the Night Angel Trilogy and the Lightbringer Series, won several industry awards, and sold a few million books.<br /><br />Brent and his wife Kristi live in Oregon with their two daughters. (Yeah, he married The Girl.)</span>
